 :D Jermey Camp is awesome!  I like your signature too ;)  Ravi Zacharias quotes Friedrich Nietzsche often.   [Rzim.org broadcasts](http://resources.christianity.com/rzim/searchItems.jhtml?JServSessionIdroot=geqwjzkl41)

[Rhythmbox Desklet](http://gdesklets.gnomedesktop.org/categories.php?func=gd_show_app&amp;gd_app_id=162)

### Post by staticactivity on 2004-10-22
You can make it start during startup. Go to
Computer -&gt; Desktop Preferences -&gt; Sessions
Choose the 'Startup Programs' tab and add 'gdesklets' to it

### Post by bvc on 2004-11-02
[QUOTE=oddabe19]My turn, I guess...

[http://home.comcast.net/~amsilveira/Ubuntu_10-26-04.jpg](http://home.comcast.net/~amsilveira/Ubuntu_10-26-04.jpg)[/QUOTE]
Hiya!
Don't know if you know it or not but you are uing the wrong size panel-bg image. Just thought I'd let you know incase you didn't already.
> ########PANEL########
The default is to use the 24 panel image.
gnome-panel images are in the $THEME/gtk-2.0 directory.
Sizes range from 24 to 48. If you want to change sizes;
-right-click the gnome-panel>properties to find out what size yours is.
-in $THEME/gtk-2.0 directory rename panel-bg.png to panel-bg-24.png,
find your size and rename it to panel-bg.png
-reset the theme


Here's my new svg theme engine theme at gnome-look and screenie :grin: 
[tesla-SVG](http://kernow-webhosting.com/~bvc/theme/screenshots/tesla-SVG.jpg)

---

### Post by Magneto on 2004-11-14
[QUOTE=panickedthumb]So is that Openbox with the gnome panel or is it just customized to LOOK like the gnome panel? If it IS the Gnome panel, I'd like to know how you switched the WM from Metacity to Openbox.

And I'd like to take a peek at your black gnome theme too, that rocks.[/QUOTE]

Thats openbox3 with only a gnome-panel running although you can use openbox instead of metacity with gnome- but my whole thing with using openbox is not using gnome.  I have a love hate relationship with gnome.

The black theme is Tenebrific and its at art.gnome.org and gnome-look.org its a gtk2 theme.

for gnome with OB3 instead of metacity 
 If you run the GNOME desktop environment:

The default window manager for the GNOME environment is metacity. To switch from metacity to Openbox, do the following:

    % openbox --replace 

Choose to save your session the next time you log out so that Openbox will be started for you when you log in again.

Note: As of GNOME 2.4, gnome-panel no longer manages its own key bindings, and requires that the window manager provide its own key bindings for showing the Main Menu and Run dialog. Openbox does this through the bundled gnome-panel-control tool, which can be used in keybindings to access the gnome-panel. Use the --main-menu option to display gnome-panel's menu, and the --run-dialog to display its Run dialog.


so you can use openbox in gnome and if u use the main-menu function the openbox menu will be the gnome menu

---

### Post by Magneto on 2004-11-14
[QUOTE=panickedthumb]Thanks magneto, and sorry for being a tool here, but how do you get the specific gnome-panel running without running gnome itself? I'd prefer to keep metacity in gnome if I can just get the panel.

And how do you call the "main-menu function" exactly?[/QUOTE]
Nah youre not bein a tool thats what this forum is for

Just run gnome-panel from a commandline or from a script- i run it from a menu script  to start the panel - if you use gnome then the panel that will appear will look the same as the gnome-panel you use within gnome  because of your user settings in ~/

Main-menu is for using openbox instead of metacity- not sure if it will work without gnome running

*****EDIT****** DO NOT START OPENBOX ALONE WITH THE main-menu option! This will cause openbox to look immediately for a running gnome/kde session and crash when none is found- you will get a session lasterd under 10 seconds popup


I never can get all the right gdesklets working so i use gnome-panel otherwise I wouldnt

### Post by HungSquirrel on 2004-12-04
```
sudo apt-get install Eterm
Eterm -f white -n DeskTerm -O -x --buttonbar false --scrollbar false
```
That makes a transparent term with no window borders or scrollbars.


> I don't know how old your SmoothDegar is, but I updated it Nov. 26th
[http://bvc.kernow-webhosting.com/th...othDegar.tar.gz](http://bvc.kernow-webhosting.com/th...othDegar.tar.gz)
Wow, it looks even better!  Well, except for the Applications and Computer menu.  The rest of my gnome-panel looks rounded and smooth, but now the buttons for that menu are flat.  Is this supposed to be this way?

[img]http://hungsquirrel.org/images/smoothdegar.png[/img]

### Post by HungSquirrel on 2004-12-10
You need to install Cedega and use it to run steaminstall.exe to install Steam.  The use Steam to download CS.

I'd sent you a direct link to the tutorial but the site has been slashdotted.  At any rate, when the dust settles, head over to [linux-gamers.net](http://linux-gamers.net).

---

### Post by bvc on 2004-12-20
[QUOTE=rwabel]Thanks for the information, I found the theme. But there is neither a README nor a gtkrc init. Can I also just install it through the gnome theme manager?

Are they also usable for XFCE?

Thanks for the help[/QUOTE]


```
localhost:~# ls .themes/Edge
NEWS  README  gtk-2.0  index.theme  metacity-1
```
the gtkrc is in .themes/Edge/gtk-2.0

No one has reported any problems so you should be able to install through the gnome-theme-manager.

They? Well, not the metacity themes. They would have to be ported. The gtk works but the statusbars in the xfce4 panel applets are really hard to see as discussed at gnome-look.

---

---

### Post by bvc on 2004-12-20
If you want the bottom round panel, in the gtkrc comment out
include "panel.rc"
and uncomment
include "panel-round.rc".

Like this;
#include "panel.rc"
include "panel-round.rc"

THEN!!! Right-click the panel>click on properties>
click on the Background tab>tick 'Background image'>
click the Browse button and select Edge/gtk-2.0/panelbg-properties.svg

you may then need to reset the theme and then
killall gnome-panel

---

### Post by bvc on 2004-12-21
[QUOTE=Rhodan]Thank you I sorted that out now.

However, when viewing the edge-flawed screenshot as posted above, my minimize/maximize/close icons do not show on windows ? Also, my gnome start icon is still the default, it is not showing as the one included in the download ? It seems the "icons" directory is not loading or something ?[/QUOTE]

There are 3 metacity themes
Edge (original and in the default download)
Edge2 (seen in the Edge-Flawed screenie -diff buttons)
Edge3 (same buttons as Edge but titlebar of Edge2)

Edge2 and 3 are also at gnome-look as an alternate download (2 metacity themes only)

the gnome-main-menu icon may not show depending on the icon theme and whether you have or may need, shouldn't have to but hey....
killall gnome-panel

I put the icon you get in the download in
Marcintesh_OS-L-White-Icons/128x128/apps
but you could do it for/with any theme, that way it is sure to be loaded either from the iconrc in the gtk theme or the icon theme.


=============
Hey TopDog, long time no see 8)

### Post by bvc on 2004-12-31
by request for a light blue somatic (mac) sorta theme ....so it's not a port just an 'inspired by' sorta thing.
[Soma](http://bvc.kernow-webhosting.com/theme/screenshots/soma.png)
It's meant to be simple but it sure seems plain to me.
If you want to check it out and PM me feedback, please do!
[http://bvc.kernow-webhosting.com/theme/test/Soma-beta.tar.gz](http://bvc.kernow-webhosting.com/theme/test/Soma-beta.tar.gz)
It's not done (and I still need a metacity) and again, there's an issue with text.
Just like with dark themes if you try a light theme with light text some things are screwy. You can easily switch these in the gtkrc to get black text. I prefer the white.
  fg[NORMAL]				= "#ffffff"
#  fg[NORMAL]				= "#000000"

here's mac's Somatic
[somatheme](http://www.dlanham.com/downloads/somatheme.htm)

### Post by wallijonn on 2005-01-09
How did you get the Ubuntu icon in place of the GNOME foot?

---

### Post by maart on 2005-01-09
[QUOTE=wallijonn]How did you get the Ubuntu icon in place of the GNOME foot?[/QUOTE]
Icon form this thread
[http://www.ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=6457](http://www.ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=6457)

```
sudo cp gnome-logo-icon-transparent.png /usr/share/pixmaps/gnome-logo-icon-transparent.png
```

Reboot

---

### Post by Sensebend on 2005-01-10
[QUOTE=maart]
Reboot[/QUOTE] A reboot is not necessary, just restart your X server with ctrl + alt + backspace.

---

### Post by senectus on 2005-01-10
[QUOTE=Sensebend]A reboot is not necessary, just restart your X server with ctrl + alt + backspace.[/QUOTE]

You don't even need to do that (as that will kill off any app you have open) just open up a cmd line and type:
killall gnome-panel

that will kill it and restart it, leaving the rest intact..  =D>

---

### Post by wallijonn on 2005-01-10
[QUOTE=maart]Icon form this thread

```
sudo cp gnome-logo-icon-transparent.png /usr/share/pixmaps/gnome-logo-icon-transparent.png
```

Reboot[/QUOTE]

```

sudo mv /usr/share/pixmaps/gnome-logo-icon.png /usr/share/pixmaps/gnome-logo-icon-old.png
sudo cp gnome-logo-icon-transparent.png /usr/share/pixmaps/gnome-logo-icon.png

```
?  

Or is there another way to set it?

### Post by oddabe19 on 2005-01-19
[QUOTE=Rotarychainsaw]I have that. But I dunno. Maybe google, duh2me.

*edit googles not helping me. I should also say I know there is the option in the properites to make it reansparent but only the middle turns clear wile all the applets still have a background. Off to play.[/QUOTE]
 right click the bar, goto properties, in the background tab, goto 'solid colour' and move the bar.

poof, you're done.

BTW, it was in every Gnome since 2.0, iirc

### Post by axcairns on 2005-01-29
No windows - 

[[IMG]http://img192.exs.cx/img192/2578/empty8ih.th.png[/IMG]](http://img192.exs.cx/my.php?loc=img192&image=empty8ih.png)

With firefox -

[[IMG]http://img195.exs.cx/img195/5654/firefox7ql.th.png[/IMG]](http://img195.exs.cx/my.php?loc=img195&image=firefox7ql.png)

The iconbar at the bottom, the clock at top left and the Seti monitor at bottom left are gDesklets. I shifted the window list, trash and pager into the top panel and got rid of the bottom panel.

The other monitors are Gkrellm. I have three sets of monitors running - one for this box (playpen) and two others for my servers (fivestar and library).

The GTK2 theme is OSX-Aqua which I found at gnome-look.org. I think I found the wallpaper there as well.

The firefox theme is Noia 2.0 Extreme. Not really happy with it but I haven't found a theme that gels with the GTK2 theme yet.

Also, a tip for posting screenshots - [www.imageshack.us](www.imageshack.us) do free hosting and allow you to do a thumbnail/link like mine above.

Cheers,

Allan

### Post by axcairns on 2005-01-30
[QUOTE=bitfoo]yeah Studio TwentyEight.  

I can install gDesklets with apt-get but I guess all my themes are broken since it never shows up and there are tons of errors about "border_whatever.png" Whatev. :|[/QUOTE]

How are you starting gDesklets? I had trouble launching the displays via Nautilus so I just opened a gnome-terminal and -

```
cd /usr/share/gdesklets/*displayname*
gdesklets *displayname.display* 
``` 

Substitute the name of the display for displayname above.

Apologies if the directory is not quite right - not in front of the box right now.

Worked a treat.

Allan

---

### Post by Josh101 on 2005-02-04
Here is my fluxbox screenshot running on my mac: [IMG]http://www.ashu39.dsl.pipex.com/screenshots/screenshot.jpg[/IMG]

I suppose you must think, "why on earth is he using fluxbox when he could be using gnome?" well its quite simple, im one of those people who have about 12 programs open at any give time so i like to have all the ram & cpu focusing on the programs rather than the desktop environment.

In case your interested:
The background is a modified version of the butterfly gdm theme and the fluxbox theme is "sn33z" which i modified to fix the fonts see [the fluxbox documentation](http://www.fluxbox.org/docbook/en/html/faq.html#AEN989) . The xmms skin is actually winamp classic from the winamp skin page.

---

### Post by Randabis on 2005-02-04
[QUOTE=LongTooth]Randabis, a little more input please. I too just install XFCE 4.2 on my test box. I'd like to know more about it. Love what you did to the panel and the terminal. How'd you do that? Any good sites for jazzing up a XFCE 4.2 installation? Let us know. Thanks.[/QUOTE]

The panels, used a gtk+ theme called RPanther2, window borders are Agua. The icons are GnomeApple. I added applets to the bottom panel for net, cpu, memory, and swap activity, as well as uptime. For the terminal I installed Terminal, and edited the preferences to use full transparency, no window borders, no scrollbar, and no menubar. 

I've now slightly changed it a little.

[http://img221.exs.cx/img221/4492/desktop2eh.jpg](http://img221.exs.cx/img221/4492/desktop2eh.jpg)

edit: here's a shot with galeon opened

[http://img215.exs.cx/img215/9330/galeonshot7rd.jpg](http://img215.exs.cx/img215/9330/galeonshot7rd.jpg)

### Post by kassetra on 2005-02-17
The ones in my app menu are a mix of recolored gartoon, gorilla, plastic suse, and industrial (I'm never happy with one theme, so I make my own!)
 
 The ones in my nautilus are:
 toolbar: semi-dynamically recolored gorilla svgs + suse plastic
 spinner: dancing ubuntu beta, with issues
 filesystem: semi-dynamically recolored gorilla folders and emblems with fruity hearts, suse plastic, and ximian xd2
 
 essentially, all of them together are "kass' theme" heh  -- I always have at least one theme folder on my system for my "favorite" icons / color schemes / metacity theme, etc.

---

### Post by wulf on 2005-02-25
I like the idea of using "wood" as your desktop image - a nice pun (especially if, as I do, your office is furnished with plastics and metal)... I'll have to bear that in mind when I'm ready for a change. Without checking back, I think what I'm using now is similar to what I posted earlier in the thread:

[[img]http://www.basswulf.plus.com/images/screenshot20050225-small.png[/img]](http://www.basswulf.plus.com/images/screenshot20050225.jpg)

However, I've now moved my panel to the right hand edge, with a few pop-out drawers for things like the window list and menus. It gives my workspace a more vertical alignment, lets me keep gkrellm in view while not sacrificing any vertical space and puts the applications I commonly need in easy reach (I'm right handed). - it's not just about prettification but also ergonomics!

Wulf

### Post by Gary Powers on 2005-02-28
Two questions:  In deference to dial up users, how does one post a thumbnail linking to a larger image and ....

I seem to be the only one who is unable to install the gDesklet "Good Weather".  Not sure how to handle the INSTALL_GOODWEATHER_SENSOR.BIN file.  The basic gDesklet package is intalled and working under Hoary.  Anybody out there who can point me in the right direction?  Thanks.

Gary

---

### Post by NeoChaosX on 2005-03-01
[quote=Gary Powers]I seem to be the only one who is unable to install the gDesklet "Good Weather". Not sure how to handle the INSTALL_GOODWEATHER_SENSOR.BIN file. The basic gDesklet package is intalled and working under Hoary. Anybody out there who can point me in the right direction? Thanks.[/quote]

Open it through console. Go to the directory the Install_GoodWeather_Sensor.bin file is and enter in "sh ./Install_GoodWeather_Sensor.bin" to install the sensor. Then you can run the GW desklet. That's how I got it working in Warty.

And you can get thumbnails for images by hosting your pictures at [ImageShack](www.imageshack.us).

---

### Post by oddabe19 on 2005-03-09
Time to go ahead and post a new one. Sorry for the Applications menu, I took this screening for a forum post. about the new menus.

[IMG]http://home.comcast.net/~amsilveira/screenie.jpg[/IMG] 

Consists of:

Mac OSX theme (GTK) from [http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php?content=13548](http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php?content=13548)

The Metacity is actually a different version... RJaguar from [http://aqua-look.org/index.html](http://aqua-look.org/index.html)

Wall paper is one from a google search of 'osx wallpapers'

Icons are actually Excuisite from here 
[http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php?content=16006](http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php?content=16006) because the OSX ones seemed too... bleh....

And the bottom panel is just a regular panel set to transparent. Gdesklets is too unreliable for me, and so i like this better.

And beep media player skin is Aqua from winamp's website.


whew... :-P

### Post by robtotheb on 2005-03-09
Why do so many people try to copy the OSX look?  It’s nice but designers at Apple are forced to make everything look metallic or white to fit the trendy brand image.  In OSX they don’t even give you a choice to change the background colour to a non-apple colour. Lets try and keep to creating some original & creative desktops (I have seen many great ones in this thread) to show our Apple loving friends and convert them to artistic freedom!

### Post by TravisNewman on 2005-03-09
[QUOTE=steffen]How did you get the bottom panel to only show icons and no text? And get the buttons themselves to be transparent?[/QUOTE]
 Those are just launchers. If you make the top panel transparent in a default install you'll notice that the launchers are transparent. he just moved them to the bottom and made his window list/task bar/whatever you wanna call it  show on the top panel instead.

### Post by bored2k on 2005-03-18
[QUOTE=telmo]Hey... very nice!
can you tell me what are those apps? I WANT THEM!  :twisted:[/QUOTE]
 The music player is muine, you can get it through apt :D .

The mount manager [down-left] is xffstab, its a very useful application XFcE has [if you are ever  installing xfce, make sure you  use the official apt for latest build -4.2.1- **deb [http://soulmachine.net/debian](http://soulmachine.net/debian) unstable/**]

The "web browser" is a terminal running elinks browser [its awsome]. Also acquired through apt.

The bittorrent manager is the official Bittorrent 4.0 from [http://www.bittorrent.com/](http://www.bittorrent.com/) .

> 6. Go easy on the images, they may help to explain something more clearly or indicate a problem you are experiencing better but you have to remember that not everyone has the same amount of bandwidth to waste on downloading large image files. If you feel you have to post images, make sure that they're properly compressed and no more than 80KB at the absolute most.

What he means is your pictures are in the 700+kb to big for the web, they should be optimize for the web down in the 100 kb give or take a few for faster loading, I have dsl didn't take to long but long enough.
Now the person with a 56k modem will be... well let say not to happy over 1.4 mb to download very slow for him.
Hope this makes you understand.

### Post by farruinn on 2005-03-18
Ok, so here's E17 with ALL the modules loaded ;-):
[http://www2.potsdam.edu/sprang31/e17screenshot.png](http://www2.potsdam.edu/sprang31/e17screenshot.png)
It really slowed my system to a crawl with it's poor little Rage 128 card, but I loaded all the modules that I could and opened a few apps so you could see that the drop shadow was on (I had turned that off because it was just slowing down my system, forgot about it).

Here's the E16 screenshot:
[http://www2.potsdam.edu/sprang31/e16screenshot.png](http://www2.potsdam.edu/sprang31/e16screenshot.png)
The enlightenment theme is called Shade and I'm using it with the industrial gtk theme (I like a clean interface). You can see that I've got engage opened here as well and in the standalone version (non e17 module version) it has some added features such as iconifying windows.  I left the iconbox open so you could see that's what it is.  I've also got two enlightenment foundation library apps open: Evidence the file manager and Entice the picture viewer.  They're pretty slick apps.

E17 is only available through cvs (I built it this morning) so I'm guessing the verison of enlightenment you've used before was E16 at the greatest.  Most of the libraries are debianized so it's just a simple matter of going through and doing debian/rules build ; debian/rules binary, install the *.deb's and keep going.  Some of the debian/control files are messed up though and make the packages have the wrong dependencies, so you'll have to watch out for that if you build it the debian way.  Honestly though I think that if/when I build cvs again I'll just put it all into /usr/local/.  It's kind of a mess having some of the stuff controlled by debian packages and the rest installed in /usr/local.

Anyway, that post is quite long enough, ta!

---

### Post by bvc on 2005-03-20
k...I confess....I secretly like the xp look :mrgreen: 
just joking but I thought I'd let those that do know about this if they don't already and those that like skinning with pixmaps have their work cut out for them. I haven't the time anymore.
-dead link-
(look at the treeview!!!) ..oh, and nice progressbar to

Get this
[http://benjamin.sipsolutions.net/experience/gtk2-engines-experience_0.9.2_i386.deb](http://benjamin.sipsolutions.net/experience/gtk2-engines-experience_0.9.2_i386.deb)
and install with
dpkg -i gtk2-engines-experience_0.9.2_i386.deb
and install this to .themes
[http://themes.freshmeat.net/projects/experience/](http://themes.freshmeat.net/projects/experience/)
See the README and colorscheme file. You can make and change color schemes with the rpl pkg/command.
[don't get the a.g.o pkgs as they are out dated ...as usual]

It is slow but if it is optimized equal to or beyond the pixmap engine it will rock, so you gtk coder's...go contrib! ...Please :mrgreen: 

icons are here
[http://art.gnome.org/themes/icon/768/](http://art.gnome.org/themes/icon/768/)

### Post by bgrant75 on 2005-03-23
Hi,

Have been using Ubuntu for sometime now and finally ditched M$ for good. Even at work. As you will see from my Screenshot I use Citrix to connect to my work. systems. Also I had to create some scripts to mount and unmount M$ fileshares.

I use a HP NC6000 notebook and have most things working. The ath0 simply works and this is great, Simply Mepis and DSL are the only other distro's I know that have MADWIFI support out of the box.

At the desktop level I use Evolution to connect to my Exchange Server and use OpenOffice for everything else...aw don't forget the fox...

I'm a IT Reseller so several of my suppliers sites i.e. HP and Acer aren't Fox freindly.

My options are unlimited now thanks to this product.

Ubu is great.

### Post by spoetnik on 2005-03-24
My Current desktop.
iBook G4 1024*768
I have "stolen" the icons en the theme from the fedora art-work team.
Download the RPM-file from the fedora project, extract it using ' alien' and copy the icons and themes to your .icons and .themes folder.

### Post by bvc on 2005-03-25
Updated the Big_Pack again :shock: 
[http://home.houston.rr.com/bvc/gtk/Clearlooks-Big_Pack-0.5.tar.bz2](http://home.houston.rr.com/bvc/gtk/Clearlooks-Big_Pack-0.5.tar.bz2)

New color scheme is Clearlooks-4Humans
[I know it is Human Beings but I though it to be too long for a theme] Color scheme is a mod of Ubuntu's (Clearlooks) Human theme. Where Ubuntu made the buttons a little lighter, I've made them a little darker. I also did the same for other widgets like 'combobox' allowing the scrollbars to remain the normal background color.

There is also a new modified Clearlooks-Coffee called Clearlooks-Decaf_Coffee. With the same changes as above, among other things.

Have Fun!

---

### Post by bvc on 2005-03-26
k... :oops: 
I've now done the same with Clearlooks, Clearlooks-Olive and Clearlooks-DeepSky. In the Big_Pack, they are called ClearlooksM, Clearlooks-OliveM, and Clearlooks-DeepSkyM (M=Modified). Someday, I'll be finished polishing all the others I've done/removed/whatever and we'll have a Huge_Pack :razz: 
Until then, I can not apologize for all the updates :mrgreen:

### Post by artnay on 2005-03-26
[QUOTE=mfs9]Another Linux-newbie. Just got my Ubuntu up and running a few days ago. I have never tried Linux before but everything has been going smoothly.

I was just wondering what audioplayer is that and what style are you using? Both look pretty neat.[/QUOTE]

As hard_i already replied, at the time I took that shot I was using rhythmbox as a media player. The icon bar and the media player control thingie on the desktop are both gDesklets powered (starterbar and rhythmlet as displays). Theme is Ana or Wintah, can't remember.

So I had some more spare time, and [this](http://users.evtek.fi/~jirig/desktop.png) is what I did.

It's quite a mix: Metacity/GNOME as a WM, Rhythmbox Applet added to panel, font ae_nice, theme is Clearlooks (Controls: Ana, Window border: Wintah, Icons: Suede). The mask on the background is originally made by archibald, I just added some shades there. Also wrote the text and added Ubuntu logo.  I decided to remove gDesklets because I encountered some usability problems with starterbar. I just added a new gnome-panel and some launchers to it. Now I can hide the icon panel easily, and vice versa. Messing around with the GUI is a never ending project to me.  :mrgreen:

### Post by digby on 2005-04-02
It's a KDE program called superkaramba.  (If you're using Gnome, the equivalent is gdesklets, but you'll have to figure it out for yourself.)

$sudo apt-get install superkaramba

That's the base.  The actual weather app is called [Liquid Weather]("http://www.kde-look.org/content/show.php?content=6384") and came from kde-look.  Untar it to wherever you like (I use /opt/superkaramba/themes/).

Then just run $superkaramba and open the theme.

### Post by TravisNewman on 2005-04-03
The blue frog in my screenshot, as has been pointed out, is azureus.

The penguin in the top panel is an applet called "gnubiff" which is available through the ubuntu repositories. You may need to enable universe, not sure.
It's an email checking applet. It can work as a standalone program, so you can put it anywhere, or it can be the applet. I have it set up to have an animated png of tux jumping when I have mail, and one of tux sleeping when there's no mail. Both animated pngs are included, you just have to change it to these through the prefs.

---
